## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermomechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which directly indicates a constitutive law for a solid under mechanical loading with temperature-dependent elastic/plastic response. Common relationships include temperature-dependent elastic modulus, thermal expansion (stress-free strain shift), and temperature-softened flow/strain-hardening laws.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelasticity (T-dependent modulus): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (small-strain elastic response with modulus changing with temperature)
- Thermal strain offset (free thermal expansion): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain after subtracting thermal expansion strain)
- Polynomial modulus in temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (empirical E(T) for limited temperature ranges)
- Exponential thermal softening of modulus: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) * epsilon (rapid stiffness loss with temperature)
- Nonlinear elastic correction: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**2) * epsilon (odd nonlinear elasticity capturing stiffening/softening vs strain)
- Power-law (Hollomon-type) hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic flow / work hardening after yield, when strain is plastic-like)
- Ludwik-type hardening with offset: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield/initial stress plus hardening term)
- Voce-type saturation hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (stress approaches an asymptote at large strain)
- Logarithmic hardening (mild strain hardening): sigma = c0 + c1 * log(1 + c2 * epsilon) (often used for metals over moderate strain ranges)
- Thermally softened hardening (separable): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(-c3 * T) (flow stress decreases with temperature at fixed strain)
- Thermoelastic + plastic-like blend (additive): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**c3 (elastic part plus nonlinear strain hardening part)
- Finite-strain (neo-Hookean-like) structure using engineering strain: sigma = c0 * ((1 + epsilon) - c1 / (1 + epsilon)**2) (captures geometric nonlinearity at larger strain)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain elastic regime → sigma proportional to epsilon, with the proportionality treated as an effective modulus E(T).
- Thermal expansion under constraint → sigma depends on a shifted strain (epsilon - c * (T - T0)); stress can be near zero along the free-expansion line.
- Temperature-induced softening → decreasing E(T) or decreasing flow stress with T, often represented by factors like (c0 + c1 * T) with c1 < 0 or exp(-c * T).
- Plastic/work hardening → sigma grows sublinearly or superlinearly with epsilon; power-law or log forms encode different curvature (concave vs convex hardening).
- Hardening saturation at large strain → sigma approaches an upper bound; (1 - exp(-c * epsilon)) is a common mechanism for asymptotic saturation.
- Elastic–plastic transition without an explicit yield variable → additive mixtures (linear-in-epsilon term plus nonlinear term) can mimic an apparent yield then hardening.
- T–epsilon coupling from thermodynamic free energy → cross terms in W(ε,T) lead to sigma containing products like epsilon * T (effective modulus or offset varying with T).
- Finite-strain nonlinearity → dependence on (1 + epsilon) and inverse powers can appear when converting from stretch-based hyperelasticity to engineering-strain variables.
